    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({

<span id="freeTextContainer6130956903088901649">Following the grief and horror of her discovery of Jack the Ripper's true identity, Audrey Rose Wadsworth has no choice but to flee London and its memories. Together with the arrogant yet charming Thomas Cresswell, she journeys to the dark heart of Romania, home to one of Europe's best schools of forensic medicine... and to another notorious killer, Vlad the Impaler, whose</span>
  <span id="freeText6130956903088901649" style="display:none">Following the grief and horror of her discovery of Jack the Ripper's true identity, Audrey Rose Wadsworth has no choice but to flee London and its memories. Together with the arrogant yet charming Thomas Cresswell, she journeys to the dark heart of Romania, home to one of Europe's best schools of forensic medicine... and to another notorious killer, Vlad the Impaler, whose thirst for blood became legend.<br /><br />But her life's dream is soon tainted by blood-soaked discoveries in the halls of the school's forbidding castle, and Audrey Rose is compelled to investigate the strangely familiar murders. What she finds brings all her terrifying fears to life once again.<br /><br />In this New York Times bestselling sequel to Kerri Maniscalco's haunting #1 debut Stalking Jack the Ripper, bizarre murders are discovered in the castle of Prince Vlad the Impaler, otherwise known as Dracula. Could it be a copycat killer...or has the depraved prince been brought back to life?</span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer2141354846" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18094383632138992880">Shoutout to me for making it through this book!<br/><br/>Seriously. If you’re looking for a better substitute for humor, mystery and general fulfillment, look no further than: <b>Buzzfeed Unsolved</b>.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2749975305" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2749975305" />
    <a title=" Teodora " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/69603149-teodora"><img alt=" Teodora " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1582144281p2/69603149.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2749975305?book_show_action=true">Jul 18, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title=" Teodora " class="user" itemprop="url" name=" Teodora " href="/user/show/69603149-teodora"> Teodora </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/69603149-teodora?shelf=on-app">on-app</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/69603149-teodora?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/69603149-teodora?shelf=historical">historical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/69603149-teodora?shelf=mystery-thriller">mystery-thriller</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2749975305" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6030612344775629564">3/5 ⭐<br/><br/>Okay so. Romanian here.<br/><br/>99% sure I’m not a vampire, but some of y’all seem to believe that everyone in Romania is from Transylvania and we all have fangs and hate garlic with a passion so you make me question my initial statement with your fairytale determination.<br/><br/>I still haven’t discovered my fangs though, but now if I think on it I might have put them into a glass of water somewhere in my mountain castle and forgot about them. Whoops.<br/><br/>Now, moving to the actual review, I have to say it: I did</span>
  <span id="freeText6030612344775629564" style="display:none">3/5 ⭐<br><br>Okay so. Romanian here.<br><br>99% sure I’m not a vampire, but some of y’all seem to believe that everyone in Romania is from Transylvania and we all have fangs and hate garlic with a passion so you make me question my initial statement with your fairytale determination.<br><br>I still haven’t discovered my fangs though, but now if I think on it I might have put them into a glass of water somewhere in my mountain castle and forgot about them. Whoops.<br><br>Now, moving to the actual review, I have to say it: I didn’t really like this (because I am biased af), but it wasn’t entirely that bad. <br><br>I didn’t know exactly how to grasp the general atmosphere of the book from the first few chapters. Because this book’s action was supposed to be set so close to where I actually live in Romania, I kind of know the geography of the place. I kind of got lost at some point while reading this…<br><br>They were talking about Bucharest and the snow-capped Carpathian Mountains in the same sentence and just try to imagine my confusion because, let me tell you, <i>Bucharest is nowhere near any mountain</i>. It’s a meadow all the way. Not to be rude or offend my friends from Bucharest (hello there, frumoșilor 👋), but people there have no idea how a snow-capped mountain is supposed to look like as seen from the window of their flat. Trust me, I lived there for three years, haven’t seen a hint of mountain.<br><br><blockquote>
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1594299380ra/29785681.gif" width="366" height="201" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</blockquote><br>Another super confusing thing for me – Audrey Rose and Thomas were planning on taking a carriage from Bucharest to the Bran Castle (which btw has nothing to do with Dracula but I will just let the rumour fly around anyway) after the Orient Express arrived at its destination. Again, how? In 1880-ish Romania, such a trip with a carriage was supposed to be at least a week long. It is a freaky almost-four-hour-trip-depending how-fast-you-drive now, in modern times, highways and all.<br><br>I am definitely being too judgemental here, it is only fiction after all, but this is the first time something like this really bothered me. Bear with me, a sister is trying to cut back on judgement and it is hard.<br>(Don’t do like me people. It’s just fiction and in fiction, people can write whatever the hell they want if they feel like it. This is just me being a total bitch).<br><br>What I thought was quite all right was the fact that the book was seasoned with various Romanian words and phrases that were, in fact, correct. And it was somehow kind of accurate because us Romanians (I’m going to generalise now, don’t kill me) tend to throw in a word in Romanian or two when we’re speaking just because sometimes we don’t really know how to find its best equivalent in English. We don’t really give a shit if the other people do not understand it, we just throw it in there and move on.<br><br><blockquote>
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1594299380ra/29785682.gif" width="386" height="212" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</blockquote><br>The plot was easy to follow and the mystery was definitely super easy to solve (at least for me). I still haven’t decided if I am glad that I knew who the criminal was here from the first chapter I met them or I am kind of annoyed that it was so obvious and I wasn’t surprised at all when everything unravelled.<br><br>What is <i>beton</i> though (aka <i>concrete</i> aka Romanian for super cool) is that there is some interesting <b>Romanian cultural insight</b> in here – there are some passages that are not really the typical facts everyone seems to know about Dracula and they are quite accurate actually (historically speaking) and there are also these little legends and mythological stories that are so damn great like, for example, Thomas’s story about the <i>strigoi.</i><br><br>Oh, and, talking about strigoi here and Thomas’s story – the story is quite real.<br><br>The strigoi are the Romanian equivalent of what the rest of the world calls vampires. In Romanian mythology (which is coming straight from the Dacian) they are the unrested souls of the undead that wake up from their own graves and roam around the villages torturing the living.<br><br>I am telling you now and I am not even joking, there have been at least two cases confirmed in modern-times Romania about rituals of killing strigoi. The traditional rituals may vary from region to region though, but people (especially those from villages who seem to still be anchored in their hundreds-of-years-old customs) still perform them. For instance, in my region when there is a strigoi case, people open the coffin of the supposed strigoi, read to them something from the Holy Bible and then they impale the strigoi’s heart with a thick wooden stake.<br>Thomas’s version of the story is actually something that happened some time in the ‘90s in the region of Romania called Oltenia. If you’re curious about this macabre thing, be my guest and read this book ;)<br><br><blockquote>
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1594299380ra/29785683.gif" width="400" height="191" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</blockquote><br>This is actually a good read, but I honestly think that the problem is with me. I cannot read something that might imply my culture and be totally, 100% okay with it. I am a true Romanian, we question and dissect everything <s>because we know everything.</s><br><br>It is worth a try though. Simply because the cultural insight is kind of <i>mișto.</i><br><br>(<a href="https://urcdn.eu/styles/9baa0b11-6b81-495e-b3b2-0cf2bc195e62_original?b" rel="nofollow noopener">Book-styled</a>)</span>
  <a data-text-id="6030612344775629564" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1867109273" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1867109273" />
    <a title="Katerina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5014021-katerina"><img alt="Katerina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1470667070p2/5014021.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1867109273?book_show_action=true">Jan 05, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Katerina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Katerina" href="/user/show/5014021-katerina">Katerina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5014021-katerina?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5014021-katerina?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5014021-katerina?shelf=crime">crime</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5014021-katerina?shelf=historical-romance">historical-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5014021-katerina?shelf=2017-reads">2017-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1867109273" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16579027599582577601"><b>
  <blockquote>Delightfully morbid.</blockquote>
</b><br/>I loved <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/28962906.Stalking_Jack_the_Ripper__Stalking_Jack_the_Ripper___1_' title='Stalking Jack the Ripper (Stalking Jack the Ripper, #1) by Kerri Maniscalco' rel='nofollow noopener'>Stalking Jack the Ripper</a>. It was a book I will always hold dear, mainly because I was <b>enchanted</b> by the gloomy Victorian London ambience and <b>disturbingly fascinated</b> by the gruesome murders and their riddles. Yet <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/33784373.Hunting_Prince_Dracula__Stalking_Jack_the_Ripper___2_' title='Hunting Prince Dracula (Stalking Jack the Ripper, #2) by Kerri Maniscalco' rel='nofollow noopener'>Hunting Prince Dracula</a>, with its <b>mystifying touch</b>, with <b>lores</b> whispered by supersticious villagers and seemingly crazy professors, medieval orders and forests covered in white snow yet somehow tainted by crimson blood and chilling howls, is the reason I bow</span>
  <span id="freeText16579027599582577601" style="display:none"><b>
  <blockquote>Delightfully morbid.</blockquote>
</b><br>I loved <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/28962906.Stalking_Jack_the_Ripper__Stalking_Jack_the_Ripper___1_" title="Stalking Jack the Ripper (Stalking Jack the Ripper, #1) by Kerri Maniscalco" rel="nofollow noopener">Stalking Jack the Ripper</a>. It was a book I will always hold dear, mainly because I was <b>enchanted</b> by the gloomy Victorian London ambience and <b>disturbingly fascinated</b> by the gruesome murders and their riddles. Yet <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/33784373.Hunting_Prince_Dracula__Stalking_Jack_the_Ripper___2_" title="Hunting Prince Dracula (Stalking Jack the Ripper, #2) by Kerri Maniscalco" rel="nofollow noopener">Hunting Prince Dracula</a>, with its <b>mystifying touch</b>, with <b>lores</b> whispered by supersticious villagers and seemingly crazy professors, medieval orders and forests covered in white snow yet somehow tainted by crimson blood and chilling howls, is the reason I bowed to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/14584166.Kerri_Maniscalco" title="Kerri Maniscalco" rel="nofollow noopener">Kerri Maniscalco</a>'s <b>exquisite pen</b>.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1492434603i/22516486.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Has the Immortal Prince returned?”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>After the tragic events of Stalking Jack the Ripper, Wadsworth and Cresswell head to Romania, to attend the Academy of Forensic Medicine and Science. But the prestigious Academy hides many secrets, from dark corridors and chambers to brutally murdered corpses that indicate one thing; the Impaler Lord has returned, seeking blood. Whose blood though and why, that's a different story. Trying to reason with evidence of the supernatural while fighting the nightmares that haunt her, Audrey Rose must find some answers and give justice to those who have already perished, before her time comes to join them in the eversleeping realms of Death.<br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“There's nothing quite like the aroma of a bloaded corpse to get one in the mood for adventure.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>My dear Mr. Thomas Cresswell cound not be more right. From the grey streets of Victorian London, Kerri Maniscalco transferred us to Romania, and painted with her colourful palette Dracula's castle and picturesque villages, blending red with white. <b>White</b> for the blinding snow. For the innocence lost. For the shroud that covered the victims of a villain utterly terrifying, that made your stomach churn with disgust and terror. <b>Red</b> for Wadsworth's lips, lips that craved to taste Cresswell's with a searing need. Red for the Prince of Blood, and his horrendous domain. For the autopsies performed by brilliant students who could not shut down their humanity. The atmosphere was <b>eerie</b>. <b>Foreboding.</b> Danger lingered in every corner. Everyone was a suspect, and everyone a potential victim. There were many times I wished for Ms. Harvey's traveling tonic to help me steel my nerves and keep reading. But in this <b>deadly and macabre puzzle</b> that gave you gooseflesh and toyed with Wadsworth's (and your very own) sanity, between the constant <b>suspense</b> and the legends of warrior societies and a brutal Prince worshipped by his countrymen, Kerri Maniscalco managed to ease the tension and make your lips curl up with mirth.<br>I suspect you already know the reason. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1419948418ra/13149808.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“I have a feeling you haven't invited me here for kissing. Though it never hurts to ask. You're dressed for sneaking about Dracula's castle. Be still my thawing, dark heart. You certainly know how to make a young man feel alive, Wadsworth.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>And along this <b>witty and charming duo</b>, you also felt alive. Belly rumbled with laughter, heart that pounded rapidly with the snarky dialogues that oozed sarcarm yet tenderness and affection at the same time, lungs that ran out of air when tension was too much to handle, Cresswell and Wadsworth are a couple the likes of which you haven't encountered so far. Wadsworth struggled with her demons, and the wounds the events of the previous book were raw and fresh, depicted in a powerful and devastating way. I won't lie and say that I was on board with every decision Wadsworth made. I think that she could become so fixated on her independence that she misinterpreted the attempts to protect her as actions to cage her, and she could be really unfair towards Cresswell. But she came a long way overcoming her emotional trauma, and her development was evident. Her sharp mind and equally sharp tongue make her a remarkable heroine.<br><b>Now let's talk about Cresswell.</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1501703377ra/23487090.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“You've stared fear in its nasty face and made it tremble. You will make it through this, Wasdworth. We will make it through this. That is a fact more tangible than any dream or nightmare. I promised I'd never lie to you. I intend to honor my word.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>As my dear friend <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/7734134-nastassja" rel="nofollow noopener">Nastassja</a> once said, Mr. Thomas Cresswell turns bloody and creepy into sexy so, so easily. While his social skills are still rusty, and his good intentions don't always work out as planned, his arrogant and (completely) inappropriate remarks, his flirtatious ways and the intensity of his feelings towards Wadsworth make him <b>utterly delectable</b>. Their scenes crackled with pent-up tension, and you couldn't help but pant a little even when there was no touching involved. Only heated stares. Innuendos. Sinful thoughts. And a love deep and powerful. From every challenge, they emerged stronger. Together and as individuals. <b>I think I'm in love with them both. </b><br><br>All in all, <b>a delicious and macabre tale, with the perfect blend of suspense, horror, Romanian folklore and sparking romance, Hunting Prince Dracula surpassed its predecessor and established Wadsworth and Cresswell as the new hot duet of crime solvers!</b><br><br><b>*ARC generously provided by the publisher in exchange for an honest review*</b><br><br><i>You can find <a href="http://booknest.eu/reviews/8-kat-reviews/703-huntingprincedracula" rel="nofollow noopener">this</a> review and more over on <a href="http://booknest.eu/" rel="nofollow noopener">BookNest.eu</a>!</i><br><br><blockquote>
  <a href="http://www.clker.com/cliparts/5/9/8/6/12279736882009934397twoton_Dividing_Line_3.svg.med.png" rel="nofollow noopener">
    <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379788972i/516772.png" alt="Dividing Line clip art" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  </a>
</blockquote><br><br><b>
  <u>BEFORE</u>
</b><br>Delightfully morbid, with the perfect blend of suspense, horror, Romanian folklore and sparking romance, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/33784373.Hunting_Prince_Dracula__Stalking_Jack_the_Ripper___2_" title="Hunting Prince Dracula (Stalking Jack the Ripper, #2) by Kerri Maniscalco" rel="nofollow noopener">Hunting Prince Dracula</a> surpassed its predecessor and established Wadsworth and Cresswell as the new hot duet of crime solvers!<br><br>Full review to come!</span>
  <a data-text-id="16579027599582577601" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2353863691" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2353863691" />
    <a title="Emma Giordano" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30604861-emma-giordano"><img alt="Emma Giordano" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1569693958p2/30604861.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2353863691?book_show_action=true">Apr 27, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emma Giordano" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emma Giordano" href="/user/show/30604861-emma-giordano">Emma Giordano</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2353863691" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14715523204043781969">As I was not a huge fan of <i>Stalking Jack The Ripper</i>, I was unsure if I would continue with the series until hearing rave reviews of book two, especially from people who also did not enjoy the first installment. I did enjoy <i>Hunting Prince Dracula</i> more than book one, but it still just wasn’t for me.<br/><br/>CW: murder/gore, sexism, ptsd<br/><br/>My absolute favorite part of this series is the characters and romance. I wasn’t the BIGGEST fan of Audrey Rose in book one, but I actually loved her in book two. I adore he</span>
  <span id="freeText14715523204043781969" style="display:none">As I was not a huge fan of <i>Stalking Jack The Ripper</i>, I was unsure if I would continue with the series until hearing rave reviews of book two, especially from people who also did not enjoy the first installment. I did enjoy <i>Hunting Prince Dracula</i> more than book one, but it still just wasn’t for me.<br /><br />CW: murder/gore, sexism, ptsd<br /><br />My absolute favorite part of this series is the characters and romance. I wasn’t the BIGGEST fan of Audrey Rose in book one, but I actually loved her in book two. I adore her independence, her intelligence, her passion, her determination – she just has so many loveable qualities! I also love Thomas even more than I did in book one (which I didn’t think was possible.) He is analytical, witty, flirtatious, respectful and all around wonderful. I adored the development of their relationship in this installment. It is so refreshing to see a YA couple that view each other as equals. Thomas and Audrey have a fulfilling, healthy relationship and they complement each other in the best way. Their growth as a couple is the perfect slow-burn and I would honestly read anything where they are together, even if this series is definitely not one of my favorites.<br /><br />I really enjoyed the setting of this story. I’ve always loved vampire folklore so the added exploration into how these legends play into Romanian culture was fascinating. I also loved the choice to transform Bran Castle, a place of great mystery and history, as the primary location of the novel. It was equal parts enchanting and creepy.<br /><br />Truthfully, there are not many distinctive critiques I have for this novel – It’s just not a favorite of mine. I do not frequently reach for historical fiction, but the plot of this series is too intriguing for me to pass up. The prose is fine, but nothing profound in my opinion. Similarly, the mystery was “okay.” I will admit I was bored for some of the story as I feel it was extremely slow-paced up until an intense ending. I just was not as engaged as other mysteries I have read. <br /><br />While this series is overall not for me, I am glad I read book two and I definitely plan to read book three. I don’t feel it is within my capacity to love this series as much as others, but I really love the premise of each story and hope to be surprised even more by the next installment.<br /><br /><i>I received a free copy of this book from Little Brown at Book Expo 2017. I had no obligation to review this book and all opinions are my own.</i></span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3241212864" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3241212864" />
    <a title="She-who-must-not-be-named " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/106473614-she-who-must-not-be-named"><img alt="She-who-must-not-be-named " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1602257813p2/106473614.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3241212864?book_show_action=true">Jun 26, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="She-who-must-not-be-named " class="user" itemprop="url" name="She-who-must-not-be-named " href="/user/show/106473614-she-who-must-not-be-named">She-who-must-not-be-named </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/106473614-she-who-must-not-be-named?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/106473614-she-who-must-not-be-named?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3241212864" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10889053084365271561"><b> “Monsters are only as real as the stories that grant them life. And they only live for as long as we tell those tales.” </b><br/><br/>This book has really advanced from <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/40727470.Stalking_Jack_the_Ripper__Stalking_Jack_the_Ripper___1_' title='Stalking Jack the Ripper (Stalking Jack the Ripper, #1) by Kerri Maniscalco' rel='nofollow noopener'>Stalking Jack the Ripper</a> in terms of character development and plot twists.<br/><br/>The story begins with Audrey and Thomas on a train to Romania, to attend one of Europe's best forensic institutes. But as people start turning up dead with their bodies completely drained of blood, students of the Institute are on high alert and suspect that Dracula hi</span>
  <span id="freeText10889053084365271561" style="display:none"><b> “Monsters are only as real as the stories that grant them life. And they only live for as long as we tell those tales.” </b><br /><br />This book has really advanced from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/40727470.Stalking_Jack_the_Ripper__Stalking_Jack_the_Ripper___1_" title="Stalking Jack the Ripper (Stalking Jack the Ripper, #1) by Kerri Maniscalco" rel="nofollow noopener">Stalking Jack the Ripper</a> in terms of character development and plot twists.<br /><br />The story begins with Audrey and Thomas on a train to Romania, to attend one of Europe's best forensic institutes. But as people start turning up dead with their bodies completely drained of blood, students of the Institute are on high alert and suspect that Dracula himself is going about on his vampiric murder spree. With a murderer on the loose, <b> Thomas Creswell </b> and <b>Audrey Rose Wadsworth </b> must work together to investigate and put a stop to him/her.<br /><br />The romance in this book was nothing less than sheer delight. Yes, it felt slow and regressive at times, but unlike the first book, I loved how Thomas manoeuvres his way through the castle just so he could meet Audrey furtively and how they both sneak away to eerie and creepy places, risking their lives for the sake of investigation. Their loyalty towards each other touched the heavy pieces of my heart and made me want to fangirl. I love Thomas with all my heart and I don't think any amount of words will do him justice. Just when I thought I couldn't love him anymore than I already do!<br /><br />Audrey Rose comes out stronger than before. The events in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/40727470.Stalking_Jack_the_Ripper__Stalking_Jack_the_Ripper___1_" title="Stalking Jack the Ripper (Stalking Jack the Ripper, #1) by Kerri Maniscalco" rel="nofollow noopener">Stalking Jack the Ripper</a> threw her off balance, tampering with her focus and nagging at her with delusional thoughts. But despite her better judgement, she is confident of who she is and is not afraid to persist on following her dreams and passion. Being a female in an institution dominated by males, she faces harsh criticism and sneers from her fellow classmates and the Headmaster but she just brushes them off and proves them wrong. I also admire how she stands up to Thomas and saves him on countless occasions. Her ability to stand up for what is right, make her own decisions and her desire to be treated as an equal is amazing.<br /><br />The story gives us an insight on <b> Vlad The Impaler </b><br />known to be one of the most important rulers of the<b> Wallachian</b> history, also infamous for his acts of cruelty, notably impaling his enemies. <br /><br />The main plot was unpredictable as the focus kept drifting between different suspects, rendering it difficult to deduce the killer. Despite the aforementioned point, the twist isn't all that jaw-dropping. The only reaction it drew from me was "Meh.... okay". The story was moderately paced but the investigation felt slow and dragged because of Audrey and Thomas' inability to make headway in the investigation.<br /><br />Overall, it was an intriguing read that had me second-guessing various interactions and the central mystery. 3.5 ⭐️</span>
  <a data-text-id="10889053084365271561" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1969447007" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1969447007" />
    <a title="destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries"><img alt="destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1557144778p2/15335689.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1969447007?book_show_action=true">Apr 12, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]" class="user" itemprop="url" name="destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]" href="/user/show/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries">destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=otp">otp</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=review-copies">review-copies</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=owned-physical">owned-physical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=historical">historical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=the-best-of-the-best">the-best-of-the-best</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=diverse-reads">diverse-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=lgbtqiap">lgbtqiap</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=mystery-thriller">mystery-thriller</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1969447007" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10790255200395986799"><blockquote>#1: <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1974638992' rel='nofollow noopener'>Stalking Jack the Ripper</a> ★★★★★<br/>#2: <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1969447007' rel='nofollow noopener'>Hunting Prince Dracula</a> ★★★★★<br/>#3: <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2121169058' rel='nofollow noopener'>Escaping From Houdini</a> ★★★★★</blockquote><br/>Are you guys ready for some serious fangirling?! This series has utterly bewitched me.<br/><br/><b>
  <i>Perhaps it was time for fathers to teach their sons how to behave around young women. They were not born superior, no matter how society falsely conditioned them. We were all equals here.</i>
</b><br/><br/>While we got to see Audrey's feminist snark come into play a little in <i>SJTR</i>, she is loud, proud, and feminist as hell in this </span>
  <span id="freeText10790255200395986799" style="display:none"><blockquote>#1: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1974638992" rel="nofollow noopener">Stalking Jack the Ripper</a> ★★★★★<br />#2: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1969447007" rel="nofollow noopener">Hunting Prince Dracula</a> ★★★★★<br />#3: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2121169058" rel="nofollow noopener">Escaping From Houdini</a> ★★★★★</blockquote><br />Are you guys ready for some serious fangirling?! This series has utterly bewitched me.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>Perhaps it was time for fathers to teach their sons how to behave around young women. They were not born superior, no matter how society falsely conditioned them. We were all equals here.</i>
</b><br /><br />While we got to see Audrey's feminist snark come into play a little in <i>SJTR</i>, she is loud, proud, and feminist as hell in this sequel. I am so here for this! Despite struggling with PTSD from the ending of the first book (and her PTSD is represented really solidly!), when she arrives at Bran Castle, Audrey refuses to let the headmaster or any of her male colleagues look down upon her. True to her nature, she claws her way to the top despite her trauma and the scorn of the men around her.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>"Mr. Thomas Cresswell would descend into each circle of Hell if you needed him to. You are the beating heart inside his ribcage."</i>
</b><br /><br />Really, though, my favorite thing about this book was how much time we get to spend with Thomas and how much his character develops. He is shamelessly head-over-heels for Audrey, and while he occasionally slips up, his intentions are always good. He learns from each mistake along the way and views her as his equal in all ways. In a genre filled with unhealthy and/or unrealistic relationships, Kerri has written a romance that feels authentic, legitimate, exciting, and so sweet. <br /><br /><b>
  <i>His eyes were my favorite constellations to gaze at; each fleck of gold surrounding his pupils were new galaxies begging to be discovered.</i>
</b><br /><br />Audrey develops tremendously as well, and opens her heart to the possibilities of a life filled with more than just cutting open cadavers and chasing down villains. I found it really delightful to watch her come to terms with the idea that she could be a strong, feminist woman without sacrificing her emotions or blossoming romance.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>"Society at large is staggeringly obtuse. If one simply looks to others for their opinions, they lose the ability to think critically for themselves. Progress would never be made if everyone all appeared and thought and loved in the same manner."</i>
</b><br /><br />Did I mention there's a queer romance in this book? Because there's totally a super precious and adorable f/f relationship between a couple of side characters. ❤ <br /><br />If you couldn't tell already, I loved every freakin' moment of <i>Hunting Prince Dracula</i>. The setting is incredible - a creepy old castle, what more could I ask for? - and the suspense is on point. I know there were some complaints that <i>SJTR</i> threw out too many red herrings, but I don't feel that was the case at all with this sequel. I found myself legitimately considering every possible avenue for the culprit, and while the ending didn't <i>shock</i> me, I loved how everything played out. Plus, we learned some delicious secrets about Mr. Cresswell, which I really hope will come into play in the next book!<br /><br />If you enjoy YA suspense/thrillers, mysteries, gothic horror, and/or an adorable romance in bloom, I highly encourage you to pick this series up ASAP! You won't regret it.<br /><br /><i>Thank you to Jimmy Patterson Books/Little, Brown and Company for providing me with an ARC in exchange for an honest review!</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="10790255200395986799" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3202249169" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3202249169" />
    <a title="jessica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10171516-jessica"><img alt="jessica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1509983330p2/10171516.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3202249169?book_show_action=true">Feb 28, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="jessica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="jessica" href="/user/show/10171516-jessica">jessica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3202249169" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10317349460076771439">wow, i love how informative this series is. its obvious KM has put in some serious medical and historical research when writing these books. i feel like i learned so much whilst reading that i probably could go and become a coroner/medical examiner. if only it were currently the 1890s. lol. <br/><br/>im still a big fan of audrey roses character and what she stands for. i like that she continues to act upon her curiosity, even when it is perceived as unladylike. but, i mean, if i had my own thomas cresswel</span>
  <span id="freeText10317349460076771439" style="display:none">wow, i love how informative this series is. its obvious KM has put in some serious medical and historical research when writing these books. i feel like i learned so much whilst reading that i probably could go and become a coroner/medical examiner. if only it were currently the 1890s. lol. <br /><br />im still a big fan of audrey roses character and what she stands for. i like that she continues to act upon her curiosity, even when it is perceived as unladylike. but, i mean, if i had my own thomas cresswell, im pretty sure i would be doing all kinds of improper things just to be near him, too. amirite, ladies? :P<br /><br />the only reason im not rounding up my rating is because i didnt quite enjoy this as much as the first book. its probably due to the subject - ive never been interested dracula/vlad the impaler - so the frequent and extensive history given throughout the story didnt really capture my attention. <br /><br />that being said, the next installment sounds absolutely delightful, so i am more than willing to continue the series. and also because i cant get enough of my boy, thomas. <br /><br /><b>↠ <i>3.5 stars</i></b></span>
  <a data-text-id="10317349460076771439" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1980483415" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1980483415" />
    <a title="Brittney ~ Reverie and Ink" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/50044222-brittney-reverie-and-ink"><img alt="Brittney ~ Reverie and Ink" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1568991289p2/50044222.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1980483415?book_show_action=true">Aug 11, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brittney ~ Reverie and Ink" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brittney ~ Reverie and Ink" href="/user/show/50044222-brittney-reverie-and-ink">Brittney ~ Reverie and Ink</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50044222-brittney-reverie-and-ink?shelf=2017-anticipated-reads">2017-anticipated-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50044222-brittney-reverie-and-ink?shelf=favorite-couples">favorite-couples</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50044222-brittney-reverie-and-ink?shelf=absolute-favorites">absolute-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50044222-brittney-reverie-and-ink?shelf=favorite-heroines">favorite-heroines</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50044222-brittney-reverie-and-ink?shelf=arcs-i-ve-reviewed">arcs-i-ve-reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50044222-brittney-reverie-and-ink?shelf=steampunk-ish">steampunk-ish</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1980483415" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7489131081576896960"><b>
  <i>"Lead the way, Wadsworth. I'm simply along for the brute strength and charm."</i>
</b><br/><br/>Omgah. This was FANTASTIC. I loved the first book, but this one blew it out of the water. Kerri Maniscalco can WRITE. <i>(Thank you to the publishers for sending me a gorgeous arc!)</i><br/><br/>Every page was brilliant. The prose was gorgeous. I loved loved loved it. (Mind you, I had to skim some of the bloody parts-weak stomach eek!) But seriously you guys, don't miss this. <br/><br/><b>
  <i>"Flowers need plenty of water to grow. Love, too, need</i></b></span>
  <span id="freeText7489131081576896960" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>"Lead the way, Wadsworth. I'm simply along for the brute strength and charm."</i>
</b><br /><br />Omgah. This was FANTASTIC. I loved the first book, but this one blew it out of the water. Kerri Maniscalco can WRITE. <i>(Thank you to the publishers for sending me a gorgeous arc!)</i><br /><br />Every page was brilliant. The prose was gorgeous. I loved loved loved it. (Mind you, I had to skim some of the bloody parts-weak stomach eek!) But seriously you guys, don't miss this. <br /><br /><b>
  <i>"Flowers need plenty of water to grow. Love, too, needs attention and affection or else it slowly withers away from neglect."</i>
</b><br /><br />Let's start with the most important matter. <br />Thomas. Freaking. Creswell.<br /><br />Just when you think you have him figured out, well... trust me. You have no idea. He was the highlight of this book. The banter and chemistry was OFF THE CHARTS. I mean, he was pretty freaking great in the first book, but the heat between him and Aubrey Rose was multiplied ten times over here. Just because they ended on a happy note in the last does NOT mean anything loses its steam. Like wow. <br /><br /><b>
  <i><br />"Do you want to know what I think? The Truth?"<br />"Yes." He gazed unabashedly into my eyes. "Make it scandalous too. This is bit too serious for my tastes."<br /></i>
</b><br /><br />Not to mention, Thomas is hiding one little detail that makes him EVEN MORE LEGIT OH MY LORD. Ugh I can't spoil but like...ermergersh. (Seriously can someone freak out with me please?)<br /><br />Aubrey Rose and Thomas are off to attend an academy set in the Brahn Castle in Romania (Dracula's castle- yes it exists.) The setting was so flipping cool. Creepy castle with secret passageways? Check. Enchanting forest and medieval village? Check. Bits of history and rumors woven throughout? Check. <br /><br />I'll admit the story was a bit on the creepy side and I'm not really a fan of horror or macabre, but I was able to skip the bits that disturbed me easily enough. Sorry Kerri, you're brilliant with the whole cadaver scenes but ahhh I had to skim that. Either way though, the story was brilliant (have I said brilliant enough? I'm going to say it more.) I don't want to give anything other clues about the plot, but just enjoy the ride. <br /><br />But even aside from the cool-as-crap setting and the edge of your toes storyline, the character development was phenomenal. Aubrey Rose is suffering from PTSD throughout the book, and it wasn't dealt with lightly. I was a little unsure of how everything played out in the end of the last book, but I was impressed with how well it was written in this one. Thomas, on the other hand, has his own dealings that broke my heart. But even amidst it all, they find little ways to move forward. I also loved the addition of Thomas's sister who is BAMF omg. But most of all? I loved discovering everyone's secrets ahhh!<br /><br /><b>
  <i>"For there are no limits to the stars, their numbers infinite. Which is precisely why I measure my love for you by the stars. An amount too boundless to count."</i>
</b><br /><br />So all in all, this gets a glowing review from me. <br /><br /><a href="http://www.herbookishthings.com" rel="nofollow noopener">My Blog</a> ~ <a href="https://www.instagram.com/reverieandink/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> ~ <a href="https://twitter.com/reverieandink" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> ~ <a href="https://www.etsy.com/shop/reverieandink" rel="nofollow noopener">Etsy</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="7489131081576896960" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer12625583919531064363">I have always wanted to travel to Romania so it was fun to go with Audrey and Thomas =) <br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1507049728i/24077647._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Audrey and Thomas are going to study at a medical school inside of Bran Castle. Oh what joy =) <br/><br/>But along the way, while riding on the Orient Express, they find a body outside of Audrey's compartment with a stake through his heart! And thus it begins....<br/><br/>There are some wonderful new friends they meet at the school and some not so nice. <br/><br/>AND <br/><br/>more bodies show up. What is happening to these people? The towns people</span>
  <span id="freeText12625583919531064363" style="display:none">I have always wanted to travel to Romania so it was fun to go with Audrey and Thomas =) <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1507049728i/24077647._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Audrey and Thomas are going to study at a medical school inside of Bran Castle. Oh what joy =) <br><br>But along the way, while riding on the Orient Express, they find a body outside of Audrey's compartment with a stake through his heart! And thus it begins....<br><br>There are some wonderful new friends they meet at the school and some not so nice. <br><br>AND <br><br>more bodies show up. What is happening to these people? The towns people think Vlad has come back! But I know the real story =) It's a little cray, but not too much. There were some little tidbits of things that I enjoyed finding out though. <br><br>Also, Thomas finds some interesting things out about his family tree. <br><br>This was so much fun! I could just picture every little thing going on and the creepy atmosphere. Oh the joy! Well, accept when they were doing autopsies. Luckily this time around I wasn't snacking. I learned my lesson in the first book! <br><br>The next case will take place somewhere in America! I wonder what they are going to do next? I can't wait! <br><br>Happy Reading! <br><br>Mel ♥<br><br>MY BLOG: <a href="http://melissa413readsalot.blogspot.com/2017/10/hunting-prince-dracula-by-kerri.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Melissa Martin's Reading List</a></span>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26402455-sana?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26402455-sana?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26402455-sana?shelf=boring-af">boring-af</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26402455-sana?shelf=endless-pain">endless-pain</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2147549796" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer310701783903042283">Hello everyone, I would really love it if you all start addressing me as Sherlock Holmes because your girl right here, solved it. I mean I had my theories and ideas and screamed when I was right oh em gee. <br/><br/>I really didn't like the first book because it was just so dull and focusing a lot on the forensics, leaving me uninterested and bored, but this book??? was so much more intriguing and interesting. <br/><br/><b>!!!!!!Spoilers from the previous book from here on!!!!!</b><br/><br/><u>So what is this book about?</u><br/>After finding </span>
  <span id="freeText310701783903042283" style="display:none">Hello everyone, I would really love it if you all start addressing me as Sherlock Holmes because your girl right here, solved it. I mean I had my theories and ideas and screamed when I was right oh em gee. <br /><br />I really didn't like the first book because it was just so dull and focusing a lot on the forensics, leaving me uninterested and bored, but this book??? was so much more intriguing and interesting. <br /><br /><b>!!!!!!Spoilers from the previous book from here on!!!!!</b><br /><br /><u>So what is this book about?</u><br />After finding out who Jack the Ripper was and facing very disturbing events, Audrey's father let's her go to Romania to study at one of the best forensic schools with Thomas Creswell!!! Somebody is murdered on the train she's traveling on and a killer is on the loose murdering people the way Dracula did. <br /><br />●This book is honestly so great!! Audrey Rose is the perfectly, flawed and strong character. She's bullied and made fun of because of her sex. No one thinks she's capable of doing anything because she's a fucking female!! But she speaks up and doesn't back down. She proves to them that's she's just as capable as males and can do whatever the fuck they can. And it's fabulous. <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>“<i>Oh? Where in a medical dictionary does it say a woman cannot handle such things? What is a man’s soul made of that a woman’s is not? I had no idea my innards were composed of cotton and kittens, while yours were filled with steel and steam-driven parts.</i>”</b>
</blockquote><br /><br />●She's so strong and badass!!! She wears dresses and cuts open dead bodies. She shows, that as a woman she can do anything anyone else could. I honestly don't understand why it's so hard for people to just understand the fact that a woman should be treated equally as anyone else and she can do ANYTHING!!!<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>“<i>Perhaps it was time for fathers to teach their sons how to behave around young women. They were not born superior, no matter how society falsely conditioned them. We were all equals here.</i>”</b>
</blockquote><br /><br />●She has anxiety, hallucination and flashbacks of what happened in the previous book. She's dealing with the loss of her brother and mother. And tbh, that makes her so so perfect. <br /><br />●Thomas Creswell is the best person to exist. He's always teasing Audrey with dirty jokes, trying to get a kiss from her, always there to support her, HE MADE A HUGE MISTAKE!!!!!, but so does everyone because we're all humans. He goes through some incredible character development and learns so much about himself. He's a little closed off and mysterious. And he's always there to support Audrey and respects her. <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>“<i>'You are not mine to take.' He brushed his lips against mine. Softly, so softly I might have imagined them there. My eyes fluttered shut. He could persuade me to build a steamship to the moon when he kissed me. We could orbit the stars together. 'You are yours to give.'</i>”</b>
</blockquote><br /><br />I need this boy in my life. I just love how he's not portrayed as the perfect, heroic guy. Audrey here takes her own lead while he helps her. He isn't the main hero and more of a sidekick type when solving the mystery and it's perfect. She saves him multiple times and he's totally fine with that. I mean, it should be fine with everyone. <br /><br />●This book is so much more intriguing and complicated from the previous. I, personally, LOVE Romania, Vlad Tepes and the whole Vampire, Dracula thing. I remember watching this one show about the whole history of Vlad, his castle and how he was imprisoned and the gore and murder. So the mystery and plot were much more interesting.<br /><br />●Romania is beautiful and I just loved it.<br /><br />●there's!!! a!!! F/f!!!! Couple!!!! And!!!! I!!!! Love!! Them!!!!!! <br /><br /><b>Spoiler about who dunnit and how ya girl solved this case!!!</b><br /><br />/////////////<br /><br />I knew for a fact it was going to be a female because of how Maniscalco portrays woman empowerment and I realized the murderer was definitely going to be a woman. Then Anastasia's giddy, cheery behavior, taking Audrey out to the woods at night and giving her the warning of being careful, her being the headmasters daughter and also talking about how she has to prove she's good enough as a woman in their eyes. I realized she was trying to appear innocent by trying to "help" out Audrey with the case. Then when we find out she's the headmasters niece or something, we all go, nahhh she can't be it, BUT I KNEW IT WAS HERRRRRR because it's all too suspicious!!!<br /><br />I got hints that she was the murderer because of all that, but then when she "died" I was like, "aw shit, it's not her" and thought it was thomas's sister. BUT THEN AT THE END THIS BITCH IS BACK AND I WAS LIKE AW YEAH FUCKERS, I WAS RIGHT EAT ALL OF MY DUST HOLMEYYYY<br /><br /><b>SPOILER ENDS</b><br /><br />////<br /><br />So like, overall, you guys should really read it because this book gives amazing messages about feminism, equality and it's such an intriguing read!!!<br /><br />Also, I'm opening my own detective school where y'all can learn from me because I'm fabulous at this ;pp</span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=z-read2018">z-read2018</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2358517299" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13274915183474307881">3 1/2 stars, rounded up because… well, it was really entertaining, and also overall of <i>much</i> higher quality than book one. And wow, I suddenly love the two leads? <br/><br/>I’m going to be talking about this a lot in relation to <i>Stalking Jack the Ripper.</i> <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2194815288' rel='nofollow noopener'>So here’s that review.</a><br/><br/>First let’s talk about the mystery, because that was something I didn’t like in book one and… wow, I love him. The cleverness of the solution here has <i>really</i> stepped it up. I didn't guess the solution at all. <br/> <br/>Okay, for the most impor</span>
  <span id="freeText13274915183474307881" style="display:none">3 1/2 stars, rounded up because… well, it was really entertaining, and also overall of <i>much</i> higher quality than book one. And wow, I suddenly love the two leads? <br /><br />I’m going to be talking about this a lot in relation to <i>Stalking Jack the Ripper.</i> <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2194815288" rel="nofollow noopener">So here’s that review.</a><br /><br />First let’s talk about the mystery, because that was something I didn’t like in book one and… wow, I love him. The cleverness of the solution here has <i>really</i> stepped it up. I didn't guess the solution at all. <br /> <br />Okay, for the most important part, let’s talk about characters, because that is the real success of this book. I really really <i>really</i> like Thomas - I only <i>liked</i> him in the last book - and I never like love interests in books like these. He’s such a good man. There’s a scene in this book where he <i>totally</i> fucks up, and I was expecting it to be glossed over completely, but he <i>immediately</i> apologizes and doesn’t blame Audrey Rose at all. Speaking of such, <b>
  <u>I love Audrey Rose.</u>
</b> Audrey Rose is suffering from severe ptsd and I think the way she is written here is so clever, so beautiful, so stunning. I love her. And <b>
  <u>I also love their relationship.</u>
</b> Just… every scene between them is so tense. I love it. <br /><br />K, let’s talk about Same issue with the lack of discussion of colonialism in Audrey Rose’s backstory - she’s biracial and Indian and that’s really awesome but colonialism is like… not discussed at all. BUT I will say the feminism thing has improved a lot - so many of the major characters in this book are ladies and it's great. There are even side sapphics and it's what I deserved. But perhaps more in the vein of feminism, I adored the narrative around Audrey not wanting to be protected and Thomas having to learn not to violate that but being totally willing to work on his own privilege. I felt like the takedown of that was missing from book one?<br /><br />Unfortunately, I did think this one could've used some <b>
  <u>editing down</u>
</b> - it's a hundred pages longer than the first book and it really drags in the middle. Part of that is the fact that the plot points feel less convoluted and weird and thrown-in, which is good, but Kerri Maniscalco hasn't quite gotten a handle on how to make plot points that <i>aren’t</i> convoluted but are still interesting, which means there are just fewer interesting plot points.<br /><br />I think my slump ruined my enjoyment of this book a lot but also... it was good. I’m so invested in the two leads. <br /><br /><a href="https://thebookishactress.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/52545435" rel="nofollow noopener">Goodreads</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/jespergayhey" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://www.youtube.com/channel/UCVIY_GxZIuclzsIw9CLSe3g" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a></span>

<div id="review_2174383168" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Riley" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/23179211-riley"><img alt="Riley" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1601446413p2/23179211.jpg" /></a>

<div id="review_2232380724" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2232380724" />
    <a title="Cristina Monica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica"><img alt="Cristina Monica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589617514p2/14596170.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2232380724?book_show_action=true">Dec 30, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cristina Monica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cristina Monica" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica">Cristina Monica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2232380724" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11162767478535748473">Oh yes, this is what I’m talking about. I almost didn’t read this sequel, because I struggled to finish the first book, but I’m Romanian so I was curious to see how Kerri Maniscalco would present my homeland as well as its history. <br/><br/>Overall, she did a good job. Obviously she consulted with Romanian speakers because she didn’t make any mistakes in the writing of the language. Thank goodness as I really hate to have to mention when they do in my reviews and it can very much be a deal breaker in som</span>
  <span id="freeText11162767478535748473" style="display:none">Oh yes, this is what I’m talking about. I almost didn’t read this sequel, because I struggled to finish the first book, but I’m Romanian so I was curious to see how Kerri Maniscalco would present my homeland as well as its history. <br /><br />Overall, she did a good job. Obviously she consulted with Romanian speakers because she didn’t make any mistakes in the writing of the language. Thank goodness as I really hate to have to mention when they do in my reviews and it can very much be a deal breaker in some cases.<br /><br />I was interested in this mystery from day one. There are a couple of deaths under mysterious circumstances occurring and the population believes their centuries-dead Prince Vlad Dracula is behind the attacks. <br /><br />Just to make things clear, while this historical figure inspired Bram Stoker’s novel, Vlad Dracula was not a vampire. Because of the gruesome ways he employed to kill his enemies, some entertained the idea, but alas (or fortunately) he was not a creature pertaining to the fantasy world.<br /><br />But I liked that this book did indeed entertain the idea. It made me wonder if maybe someone hunted for prey as a vampire would or fancied themselves to be the latter. I couldn’t know for sure, but I was simply happy to know as much as Audrey and her sidekick did. <br /><br />It’s probably wrong for me to call him a ‘‘sidekick,’’ seeing that he is important to the story and helps find answers as much as Audrey does, but am I the only one who is tired of the sarcastic flirty comments? I’m surprised I even minded them, as I normally enjoy clever back-and-forths, but I had the feeling Thomas Cresswell tried too hard to become the next Will Herondale. <br /><br />Good thing he cares about Audrey in a truthful way, even though he makes annoying mistakes, otherwise I would not have been able to tolerate him. Perhaps the number of comments will decline in the future tomes? Eh, I doubt it. <br /><br />It was a pleasure to read this mystery. However, it is not terrifying or worth being categorized as a ‘‘horror’’ story. Only the spiders made me want to read faster, but then again I had so many spiders in my room last summer that now instead of scaring me they’re just being bothersome. In a pros and cons list, this would be a pro by the way. I prefer not to have nightmares, thank you very much. <br /><br />But to go back to the storyline, I especially enjoyed and appreciated the Romanian culture, history and folklore incorporated. No wonder I love fantasy; I come from a place with a past most peculiar. While I was eager for Audrey to undercover the identity of the murderer, I took pleasure in the journey. That’s the most important part. The ending lasts only a couple of pages, but the journey lasts a couple of hundreds of pages. <br /><br />I feel as though I understand Audrey and Thomas much, much better after today. In the predecessor, we are introduced to Audrey’s family, but in this sequel, we are introduced to Thomas’. Some lovely new faces—and some you’ll want to forget. <br /><br />I sure can’t wait to see what else the author has in store for us. To America!<br /><br /><a href="https://hitormissbooks.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/LolaReviewer" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a>Twitter</a> | <a>Instagram</a> | <a href="https://plus.google.com/u/0/105021852309973899120/posts" rel="nofollow noopener">Google+</a> | <a href="https://www.bloglovin.com/blogs/hit-miss-books-12564715" rel="nofollow noopener">Bloglovin’</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="11162767478535748473" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1765164715" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1765164715" />
    <a title="Nastassja" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7734134-nastassja"><img alt="Nastassja" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596034018p2/7734134.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1765164715?book_show_action=true">Sep 22, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nastassja" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nastassja" href="/user/show/7734134-nastassja">Nastassja</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7734134-nastassja?shelf=1st-pov">1st-pov</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7734134-nastassja?shelf=excellent-writing">excellent-writing</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7734134-nastassja?shelf=gives-me-creeps">gives-me-creeps</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7734134-nastassja?shelf=2017">2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7734134-nastassja?shelf=alternative-history">alternative-history</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7734134-nastassja?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7734134-nastassja?shelf=emotional">emotional</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7734134-nastassja?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7734134-nastassja?shelf=gives-me-goosebumps">gives-me-goosebumps</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7734134-nastassja?shelf=gothic">gothic</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1765164715" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2784325551273712545"><blockquote>
  <b>Monsters were in the eye of the beholder. And no one wanted to discover their hero was the true villain of the story.</b>
</blockquote><br/><br/>Wadsworth and Cresswell are back and this time they are hunting Dracula himself! Before starting this review I should probably mention that Stalking Jack the Ripper was one of my favorite books last year. I had an absolutely illogical crush on Thomas Cresswell, which was pretty obvious from my review (note: fangirling rumblings without stop is a better way to describe that rev</span>
  <span id="freeText2784325551273712545" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <b>Monsters were in the eye of the beholder. And no one wanted to discover their hero was the true villain of the story.</b>
</blockquote><br /><br />Wadsworth and Cresswell are back and this time they are hunting Dracula himself! Before starting this review I should probably mention that Stalking Jack the Ripper was one of my favorite books last year. I had an absolutely illogical crush on Thomas Cresswell, which was pretty obvious from my review (note: fangirling rumblings without stop is a better way to describe that review), and I cannot express with words how excited I was to read Hunting Prince Dracula. Of course, I preordered the book as soon as possible and the waiting began. Months of anticipation and teasers from the author and finally the book was in my hands! But than something unexplainable happened: I absolutely loved the gothic atmosphere of book two, I loved the mystery, which I didn't guess as soon as i did in book 1, <i>but</i> my dear Cresswell didn't make my heart jump out of my chest and didn't turn my breathing erratic as it was before. What happened, I asked myself? Was it due to the stress I am having at the moment in real life that everything feels less bright to me? But no, the answer was buried much deeper than the influence of the outside factors. Simply, Cresswell stopped to intrigue me as a character, because he lost the spark he had in book 1. What I mean is we have the same problem as many YA books before: <b>a hero turns into obedient, character-less puppy in the presence of a strong independent feminist heroine</b>. Sigh. I get that Audrey Rose is all modern and amazing, but why Cresswell's character must suffer because of it? What about strong male characters that could be equals to strong female characters? Everyone remember Rhett Butler. Huh? I don't remember him turning into a goo in the presence of a very strong Scarlett. Moreover, it seems that Cresswell lost his genius mind along with his temper. It literally explained to us because of his love for the heroine he couldn't deduct simplest of things. Well, if things has turn this way than I demand this couple to break up! If Cresswell was with me he wouldn't've lost a ounce of his geniality, that's it! Sorry for my rumble, but <b>I was extremely disappointed with Cresswell in this book</b>. I still hope book 3 will bring me back my snarky dashing hero with his geniality intact. <br /><br />Apart from some out-of-character behavior I enjoyed the story a lot. I mean: <b>Europe, Dracula's castle, secret passages, monstrous creatures and everything dashed with mystery and romance - a perfect mix to take one's mind from everyday problems.</b> I felt myself fully engaged by the storytelling and couldn't wait to find out who the main culprit was. And in the case of Hunting Prince Dracula I didn't guess the murderer as soon as I did in book 1, and it added to the level of enjoyment I received from this story.<br /><br />I am extremely curious as how the story will evolve in book 3, what will be the main theme; what legend or real life murder case the author will choose for the story. Plus, you know, the story takes place in America and it's interesting to see our beloved characters in new surroundings testing their minds and relationship.<br /><br />The writing was as perfect as in book one: <b>the words were coming alive and flying from the pages in a cadence of perfect symmetry</b>, and images were born before my eyes with a perfect clarity and a dash of morbid anticipation tickling my nerves in the best way possible (I love to test my nerves like that). I noticed more than once that I was reading some lines aloud, enjoying the way words were built into sentences and pictures in my head. Kerri Maniscalco once again proved to be a queen of storytelling. Bravo! <br /><br />If you haven't read the book yet, I don't want to give extra details about the plot. Better <b>dive into the story without knowing much about the storyline and enjoy every revelation waiting for you on book's pages</b>. As for me, I am mostly satisfied with everything, but still waiting for some improvement for my dearest Cresswell. So hopefully my fangirling over his awesomeness will be back in book 3. And for those who haven't started this series yet: just give it a chance and maybe you will find the world of Thomas Cresswell and Audrey Rose Wadsworth to your liking, and, who knows, maybe even to you adoration *wink*.<br /><br /><b>
  <blockquote>"If you were guilty and wanted to hide, where might you go first?"<br />"Depends on what I'm guilty of. Dirty thoughts or wanton follies, I'd send myself straight to your quarters to be punished."</blockquote>
</b><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="2784325551273712545" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer6531391273828920087">5 freaking stars!!!<br/><br/>If <b>Nancy Drew</b> and <b>National Treasure</b> had a book baby it would probably this book (just add gory murders). <br/><br/>If I had some issues with Stalking Jack the Ripper, this book managed to wipe all of it. It was phenomenally awesome!!! <br/><br/>The suspense, mystery, horror, adventure, and romance was superb! In the first book I had a problem with the identity of the culprit because it was too obvious, but with this book? My brain totally failed to guess the culprit. It was that surprising and go</span>
  <span id="freeText6531391273828920087" style="display:none">5 freaking stars!!!<br /><br />If <b>Nancy Drew</b> and <b>National Treasure</b> had a book baby it would probably this book (just add gory murders). <br /><br />If I had some issues with Stalking Jack the Ripper, this book managed to wipe all of it. It was phenomenally awesome!!! <br /><br />The suspense, mystery, horror, adventure, and romance was superb! In the first book I had a problem with the identity of the culprit because it was too obvious, but with this book? My brain totally failed to guess the culprit. It was that surprising and good. The setting was more exciting because I love everything about Transylvania. This place is rarely featured in books and even movies, which made me more thrilled and happy to read this book.<br /><br />I still love Audrey Rose and Thomas Cresswell in this book. Audrey was somewhat different from the girl she was on the first book. She experiences extreme sadness because what happened in the first book. Well. There is no doubt that Thomas Cresswell managed to wipe me off my feet. I really wish this dude is a real person so I can make him mine. I love him so much. I love how smart, observant, brilliant, charming, flirty, and absolutely adorable he is. <br /><br />I'm glad how the sexual frustration was solved in this book. I was half-swooning, half-frustrated with their flirting because THEY ARE A TEASE. A FREAKING TEASE. <br /><br />I can't wait to read Escaping from Houdini!</span>
