I couldn't accurately predict the killer but I'm so glad how it turned out in the end. Of course, just like in <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/28962906.Stalking_Jack_the_Ripper__Stalking_Jack_the_Ripper___1_' title='Stalking Jack the Ripper (Stalking Jack the Ripper, #1) by Kerri Maniscalco' rel='nofollow noopener'>Stalking Jack the Ripper</a>, there were lots of healthy bickering betw</span>
  <span id="freeText17453244119039452368" style="display:none">I chanted all throughout this slow paced book that I was here for Thomas Cresswell and it worked because by the time I reached chapter 38, I couldn't put it down. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/33784373.Hunting_Prince_Dracula__Stalking_Jack_the_Ripper___2_" title="Hunting Prince Dracula (Stalking Jack the Ripper, #2) by Kerri Maniscalco" rel="nofollow noopener">Hunting Prince Dracula</a> is a lot more complicated in its mystery aspect and there was just <b>so much going on</b> in the forensics institute that both leads were in. I couldn't accurately predict the killer but I'm so glad how it turned out in the end. Of course, just like in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/28962906.Stalking_Jack_the_Ripper__Stalking_Jack_the_Ripper___1_" title="Stalking Jack the Ripper (Stalking Jack the Ripper, #1) by Kerri Maniscalco" rel="nofollow noopener">Stalking Jack the Ripper</a>, there were lots of healthy bickering between Audrey and Thomas which kept the story alive and will make you want to root for them even more in this book. <br><br><a href="http://tinypic.com?ref=30cyt1k" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">

<div id="review_2146663401" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2146663401" />
    <a title="Hailey (Hailey in Bookland)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/21937982-hailey-hailey-in-bookland"><img alt="Hailey (Hailey in Bookland)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1560365354p2/21937982.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2146663401?book_show_action=true">Oct 13, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Hailey (Hailey in Bookland)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Hailey (Hailey in Bookland)" href="/user/show/21937982-hailey-hailey-in-bookland">Hailey (Hailey in Bookland)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21937982-hailey-hailey-in-bookland?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21937982-hailey-hailey-in-bookland?shelf=mystery-thriller-paranormal">mystery-thriller-paranormal</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2146663401" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer841333128010664802"><b>The Short</b><br/>Actual rating: 4.5* <br/><br/>Perfect for fans of: Stalking Jack the Ripper by Kerri Maniscalco (obviously as this is the sequel), And I Darken by Kiersten White (I haven't finished this one but it reminded me a bit of what I have read of it, mostly due to the setting)<br/><br/>Writing: 4.5 stars<br/>Characters: 4.5 stars <br/>Plot: 4.5 stars<br/>Originality: 4.5 stars<br/>(All out of 5 stars)<br/><br/><b>The Long</b><br/>This series is soooo good ahhhh. I listened to the audiobook for this one, which is what I did with the first book, and it was </span>
  <span id="freeText841333128010664802" style="display:none"><b>The Short</b><br />Actual rating: 4.5* <br /><br />Perfect for fans of: Stalking Jack the Ripper by Kerri Maniscalco (obviously as this is the sequel), And I Darken by Kiersten White (I haven't finished this one but it reminded me a bit of what I have read of it, mostly due to the setting)<br /><br />Writing: 4.5 stars<br />Characters: 4.5 stars <br />Plot: 4.5 stars<br />Originality: 4.5 stars<br />(All out of 5 stars)<br /><br /><b>The Long</b><br />This series is soooo good ahhhh. I listened to the audiobook for this one, which is what I did with the first book, and it was a great decision. The audiobooks are awesome, I highly recommend them. <br /><br />The romance is this book was excellent. I've become very low tolerance in terms of romance in YA and its tendency to highlight very unhealthy relationships (possessive language, particularly). Before I read the first book, I expected to see a relationship I would hate, but I was pleasantly surprised to find quite the opposite. In this sequel, the relationship is really unpacked. Audrey Rose's position as a proper Victorian girl is brought even further into the spotlight as she and Thomas try to find a balance in their relationship. I loved that the power balance and her autonomy became a central focus of the book. It showed how a real relationship should work, IMO. Also Thomas is the first love interest I've found incredibly swoon worthy in a LONG time. But I love him. A lot. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Although when he pretended to be dead to try and talk to her I was LIVID. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Audrey Rose is an independent, intelligent young lady that calls Thomas out on his bullshit. It's amazing. She's super headstrong and driven and you see her developing even more into the precious scholar that she is in this sequel. Watching her learn and grow as this series goes on is an absolute pleasure. She is such a great heroine. The author writes the story in a way that gives you a true sense of how her mind works, with its tendency to favour logic and analysis (very left brained). It felt like I was watching the gears turn on a well oiled machine watching her to try and piece together the mystery. She's also a very authentic character. She went through a lot in the first book and you don't see her just brushing that aside. She has to work through her newfound fears in order to do what she loves again. <br /><br />The setting in this book is where it stood out against SJTR. While SJTR did a wonderful job of immersing me in Victorian London, that's a place I've been many times (though I really do LOVE revisiting it). But this book is set in Romania and o h m y g o d THE CASTLES. I love castles and boy did this book ever have beautiful castles and just an overall enchanting setting. It was described wonderfully and it just felt like you were in a fairy tale. I loved it!<br /><br />The mystery in this was jam packed with twists and turns and I loved how it pulled from the tale of Dracula. I've yet to read Bram Stoker's Dracula (I'm hoping to before the end of the month), but I am familiar with the legend, as I feel most are. It was a delightfully spooky Halloween read with this looming question of the supernatural hanging over the whole book. Just SO good. <br /><br />Overall, this series is excellent. Fantastically written (the descriptions are ON POINT), you follow characters that steal your heart (terrible joke if you've read the first one) as they trapeze around eerie locales trying to solve murder mysteries. It is great. If you're looking for the perfect Halloween read, look no further than this series!<br /><br />I'm so sad I have to wait a whole year for the next book. <br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ This book ends with the characters heading off to America, I'm so curious what mystery the next book will tackle! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />*Thank you to Indigo for the ARC! All opinions expressed are my own, as per usual.*</span>
  <a data-text-id="841333128010664802" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1834097022" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1834097022" />
    <a title="ambsreads" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30813900-ambsreads"><img alt="ambsreads" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1508924675p2/30813900.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1834097022?book_show_action=true">Jan 03, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="ambsreads" class="user" itemprop="url" name="ambsreads" href="/user/show/30813900-ambsreads">ambsreads</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30813900-ambsreads?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30813900-ambsreads?shelf=books-i-own">books-i-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30813900-ambsreads?shelf=dark">dark</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30813900-ambsreads?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30813900-ambsreads?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30813900-ambsreads?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30813900-ambsreads?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30813900-ambsreads?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30813900-ambsreads?shelf=mental-health">mental-health</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1834097022" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10615087025101598667"><i>Thank you to Hachette Children’s Books for kindly sending me a copy to review. All thoughts are my own, however.</i><br/>TRIGGER WARNINGS: anxiety, grief, murder, gore and PTSD.<br/><br/><a href='https://ambsreads.wordpress.com/2017/09/22/hunting-prince-dracula-by-kerri-maniscalco-review/' rel='nofollow noopener'>THIS REVIEW & OTHERS CAN ALSO BE FOUND ON MY BLOG</a><br/><br/>R A M B LE<br/><br/>I try to make it known that Kerri Maniscalco is one of my favourite authors. I don’t know If I’ve made that clear, but I love her. Is that too far? She just seems like an incredible person and I am absolutely in love her writing. Hunting Prince Dracula met every expectatio</span>
  <span id="freeText10615087025101598667" style="display:none"><i>Thank you to Hachette Children’s Books for kindly sending me a copy to review. All thoughts are my own, however.</i><br />TRIGGER WARNINGS: anxiety, grief, murder, gore and PTSD.<br /><br /><a href="https://ambsreads.wordpress.com/2017/09/22/hunting-prince-dracula-by-kerri-maniscalco-review/" rel="nofollow noopener">THIS REVIEW &amp; OTHERS CAN ALSO BE FOUND ON MY BLOG</a><br /><br />R A M B LE<br /><br />I try to make it known that Kerri Maniscalco is one of my favourite authors. I don’t know If I’ve made that clear, but I love her. Is that too far? She just seems like an incredible person and I am absolutely in love her writing. Hunting Prince Dracula met every expectation I had and more. Maniscalco manages to weave a haunting and mysterious tale that incorporates romances between incredible characters. She puts her twist on historical fiction and she does it well.<br /><br />This book features some things that the first didn’t, though. We still have the feminism in place for our main character, and even more feminist characters are introduced throughout the novel. However, the events of the first book are weighing down on our main character. Audrey Rose is plagued with flashbacks to what happened (what I’m labelling PTSD) and anxiety, while also dealing with an immense amount of grief. I’ll speak more on these later, but the author deals with these particular topics in a way that is perfectly integrated into the story. The mental health incorporations are seamlessly introduced and, in my belief, treated with care as they should.<br /><br />I’m not sure what else I can ramble about. This book features a diverse cast and is one of the only historical fiction novels I can find myself sitting through without getting mad about the treatment of women. Audrey Rose and Thomas are incredible and the overall cast of characters is beyond interesting. Not a single event in this book can be viewed as filler and it is my belief that this book in no way suffers from second book syndrome.<br /><br />P L O T<br /><br />Hunting Prince Dracula is quite clearly a mystery. Our main characters are looking at becoming forensic scientists (I believe? They basically cut open dead bodies) and are now travelling all the way to Romania to further their studies. This is pretty amazing since Audrey Rose is a woman in the 1800’s.<br /><br />However, wherever our main characters go mystery follows, it seems, and soon the pair is caught up in the strange murders that are plaguing the village near them. Villagers are going missing and the legend of Dracula is returning. The puncture marks and lack of blood in any of the victim’s bodies make it easy to believe one thing; the Strigoi have returned.<br /><br />While all this is happening, Audrey Rose is struggling to come to turns with what happened in London a few weeks prior to her attending this school. The idea of another killer on the loose sends her into a spiral of fear. It was interesting to see her reactions to certain events, how she had to do her best to remain unflinching in order to be seen as an equal to her peers. I loved seeing the friendships she made and how she did her best to remain ‘a proper lady of society’ while doing things that no one of that era would approve of.<br /><br />The mystery is beautifully woven in a way that you are second guessing everyone. I worked out it was pretty early in the book but I was second guessing myself the whole way until the reveal. It was incredible. I could barely keep my draw my dropping. I was also grinning giddily in public at other parts.<br /><br />So, warning, don’t read this in public if you are afraid of people watching you.<br /><br />C H A R A C T E R S<br /><br />#A U D R E Y R O S E<br /><br />Audrey Rose is everything I want to be and more. She is an icon. I have gone through some events in my life that have lead to me being slightly untrusting and cautious of new people. However, in some ways, Audrey Rose has gone through more traumatic scenarios and still fights for her rights in a man dominated world. An absolute icon.<br /><br />Throughout this book we witness her discovering herself more. Who she is when she isn’t surrounded by people she grew up with and when the restrictions that society have placed on her seem to get left behind. It was enchanting. Can I say that? Well, I just did. I just absolutely adored seeing how she dealt with situations and viewing her struggles with her mental health.<br /><br />It was absurd, in some ways, to see struggles I face on a day to day basis reflected in another character. I don’t know. Whenever there is PTSD in a book I immediately have so much love and appreciation due to my own struggles. Especially when it’s done amazingly well. And, let me tell you, it was like Maniscalco had gone into my head and plucked thoughts and feelings to put in text. I just have no words to describe how reading a character so like me felt.<br /><br />#T H O M A S<br /><br />Thomas Cresswell is the actual love of my life. I have never read a character who I would love to meet in person (and probably fall in love with him only to be rejected, it’s how my life goes, friends). He is everything I want in a man. I truly didn’t know it was this possible to fall in love with a character. I may need to change degrees and learn how to create humans (I have no idea on science, clearly) so I can form my own Thomas Cresswell for myself.<br /><br />On a more professional note (big joke there, when are my reviews ever professional?) Thomas is an incredibly complex character. The way he develops and grows in this series. His charm, his sarcasm, his adoration for Audrey Rose. It is all so completely swoon-worthy. The fact he is merely there to be her sidekick rather than the focal point. He is okay taking the backseat and letting her drive which is a dream.<br /><br />Thomas was a tad absent this book due to mistakes he made and were dealt with amazingly, but I could still feel his presence as we learnt more about his past and how he was connected to Romania.<br /><br />Basically, I love Thomas Cresswell and I would give away all my books to find a guy like that (not really, but let’s pretend).<br /><br />O V E R A L L<br /><br />Overall, Maniscalco did it again. She has delivered another incredible story that leaves you on the edge of your seat in anticipation. She has delivered a story with a full cast of characters that will instantly become some of your favourites. She has delivered a masterpiece, in my opinion, that has immediately shot to my favourite 3 books of this year (maybe ever). I am truly anticipating book three and what I can do to wrap my greedy little hands on it despite the fact it’s only in the draft stage.<br /><br />Happy reading, everyone! And, if you have time, you need to pick up this series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10615087025101598667" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1999977103?book_show_action=true">Sep 19, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Wren (fablesandwren)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Wren (fablesandwren)" href="/user/show/42780417-wren-fablesandwren">Wren (fablesandwren)</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42780417-wren-fablesandwren?shelf=physical-shelf">physical-shelf</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1999977103" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8361490859000664928">This book just screams gloomy-enchantment. Like the ton of Van Helsing or Dracula (that’s probably the point). There’s just so much to talk about but so little that I can say.<br/><br/>Audrey Rose and Cresswell are off to study the dead at a once-castle in Romania. But from the moment they got on the train, there is a trail of murders for them to solve already. No matter where these two go, there is always a mystery to solve.<br/><br/>The worst part about this whole murder-thing is that they all look like vampires </span>
  <span id="freeText8361490859000664928" style="display:none">This book just screams gloomy-enchantment. Like the ton of Van Helsing or Dracula (that’s probably the point). There’s just so much to talk about but so little that I can say.<br><br>Audrey Rose and Cresswell are off to study the dead at a once-castle in Romania. But from the moment they got on the train, there is a trail of murders for them to solve already. No matter where these two go, there is always a mystery to solve.<br><br>The worst part about this whole murder-thing is that they all look like vampires did them. Blood drained... bite marks... garlic... the whole package is there. Heck, the castle is even infested with bats to put the cherry on the cake. So could the supernatural make an appearance in this lovely gory series?<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1506293308ra/24004054.gif" alt="" width="350" height="198" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The characters are by far the best points of this series. Audrey Rose is are protagonist and she is going through major PTSD from the last book. The author really does show that in a light that is realistic. She doesn’t use it as a tool to make you feel sorry for her or cripple her; she uses it as a growth tool. Audrey Rose has flashbacks to that awful night she discovered who was Jack the Ripper, and it wasn’t just going to go away.<br><br><b>“I have a feeling you haven't invited me here for kissing. Though it never hurts to ask. You're dressed for sneaking about Dracula's castle. Be still my thawing, dark heart. You certainly know how to make a young man feel alive, Wadsworth.”</b><br><br>Cresswell is as charming as ever. His wit is sharp but his understanding is lacking. He constantly is dealing with “I thought that you would think it was funny” or “I thought I was doing the right thing” and he is growing constantly and understanding the people around him (mainly Audrey Rose). <br><br>You also get to learn more about his past and where he came from. This whole story is just so thought out and well written. Oh! The writing! It is just a poem and weaves so well together. You get the chills down your spin from the eerie atmosphere and the gore that is so beautifully worded. <br><br>---<br><br>AHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHH RTC.<br><br>---<br><br>This is just as thrilling as the first book and I'm LIVING for it. <br><br>---<br><br>OH YOU SAY YOU HAVE A BAT PROBLEM IS THAT BECAUSE YOU'RE A VAMPIRE JUST TELL ME<br><br>---<br><br>She has such PTSD from the ending of the last book... this poor girl 💔</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer17841042954256947821">I think I'm in for the ride with this series strictly because they're fun to listen to, but the characters both got on my nerves in this book and I still think Audrey Rose is hypocritical and her feminism is often blunt and overly modern for the time period. The plot in this one wasn't as interesting as it seemed from the description, but I still love the atmosphere that Maniscalco makes with the creepiness of the basement tunnels and the dead bodies and stuff. <br/><br/>Not a huge fan of the romance beca</span>
  <span id="freeText17841042954256947821" style="display:none">I think I'm in for the ride with this series strictly because they're fun to listen to, but the characters both got on my nerves in this book and I still think Audrey Rose is hypocritical and her feminism is often blunt and overly modern for the time period. The plot in this one wasn't as interesting as it seemed from the description, but I still love the atmosphere that Maniscalco makes with the creepiness of the basement tunnels and the dead bodies and stuff. <br /><br />Not a huge fan of the romance because the angst is really choppy but i'm interested to see where it goes.</span>

<div id="review_1875017761" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1875017761" />
    <a title="Rachel E. Carter" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/29482005-rachel-e-carter"><img alt="Rachel E. Carter" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1512593159p2/29482005.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1875017761?book_show_action=true">Oct 20, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rachel E. Carter" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rachel E. Carter" href="/user/show/29482005-rachel-e-carter">Rachel E. Carter</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29482005-rachel-e-carter?shelf=have-paperback">have-paperback</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1875017761" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1475271773010251597">THAT ENDING WAS SO GOOOOD!!! I adore Creswell & Wadsworth SO. MUCH. And a total teaser for the next book, I can't wait. GOING TO AMERICA!!! <br/><br/>Also, seriously, you guys need to listen to the audiobooks for these -the narrator is FANTASTIC.</span>
  <span id="freeText1475271773010251597" style="display:none">THAT ENDING WAS SO GOOOOD!!! I adore Creswell &amp; Wadsworth SO. MUCH. And a total teaser for the next book, I can't wait. GOING TO AMERICA!!! <br /><br />Also, seriously, you guys need to listen to the audiobooks for these -the narrator is FANTASTIC.</span>

<div id="review_2137255111" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2137255111" />
    <a title="Jasmine from How Useful It Is" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4467515-jasmine-from-how-useful-it-is"><img alt="Jasmine from How Useful It Is" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1516737798p2/4467515.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2137255111?book_show_action=true">Jun 22, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jasmine from How Useful It Is" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jasmine from How Useful It Is" href="/user/show/4467515-jasmine-from-how-useful-it-is">Jasmine from How Useful It Is</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4467515-jasmine-from-how-useful-it-is?shelf=library">library</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4467515-jasmine-from-how-useful-it-is?shelf=thrillers">thrillers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4467515-jasmine-from-how-useful-it-is?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2137255111" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16288567226310458971">My Experience: I started reading Hunting Prince Dracula on 5/10/18 and finished it on 6/22/18. This book is a wonderful read! (I was in suspense for many days due to family reunion and waiting to borrow my book again from the library). I enjoy Audrey Rose and Thomas’ flirting/banter a lot. It’s interesting reading about life in 1888, where girls should keep their distance from boys and furs are heavily used as blankets. I like that they are dressed well and speak well all the time. I like how Au</span>
  <span id="freeText16288567226310458971" style="display:none">My Experience: I started reading Hunting Prince Dracula on 5/10/18 and finished it on 6/22/18. This book is a wonderful read! (I was in suspense for many days due to family reunion and waiting to borrow my book again from the library). I enjoy Audrey Rose and Thomas’ flirting/banter a lot. It’s interesting reading about life in 1888, where girls should keep their distance from boys and furs are heavily used as blankets. I like that they are dressed well and speak well all the time. I like how Audrey Rose is playing hard to get with Thomas, even though, she clearly likes him. I like how Audrey fight for a woman’s place in a men dominant world. I like her confidence and strong will to stand up, chin up, and dare the men of her presence. I like the location of the foreign country. I like how I couldn’t guess the ending and the build up leading to who it is, was tantalizing.<br /><br />This book is told in the first person point of view following Audrey Rose Wadsworth, 17, as she and Thomas Cresswell journey by train to Academy of Forensic Medicine and Science in Romania. At the end of book one, readers learned that they both will leave home to further their education in medicine, specifically focusing on examining cadavers. As soon as Audrey Rose arrives, she hears rumors about Vlad Dracula coming back from the dead and causing recent deaths to the locals. There are Romanian language speaking in this book. The school is creepy and locates in a secluded area, yet it’s prestigious and difficult to get in. Before classes begin, Audrey Rose’s fellow classmate, Wilhelm was found dead in the snow. When class starts, Wilhelm’s dead body serves as the subject for students to study. Audrey Rose volunteer to cut open Wilhelm and that’s when she discovers that Wilhelm’s blood is all drained from his body, much like how Dracula kill his victims. A mystery to solve!<br /><br />This book is very well written. I love the idea of having rumors spread about hundred-year-old killer coming back from the dead to cause havoc and then Audrey Rose working to uncover answers. I like how curious the main character is. She pushes forward even when she’s afraid to find out who, what, and why. It reminds me of Harry Potter, always looking for answers but often finding trouble before solving the mystery. It’s sure is an exciting read full of adventures though. I like the castle and those hidden passages. I like when characters come together to discuss the problem and working it out loud. It’s interesting to read about a school only accepting highborn students coming from well-known and big names family, including a Prince. I like learning a bit more about Vlad Dracula in this book too since I didn’t read other historical books of him. This series is worth reading and I highly recommend everyone to read it!<br /><br />Pro: humor, slow burning romance, fast paced, page turner, mystery &amp; suspense, actions &amp; adventures, diversity, examining cadavers, Romania<br /><br />Con: none<br /><br />I rate it 5 stars!<br /><br />xoxo, Jasmine at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.howusefulitis.wordpress.com">www.howusefulitis.wordpress.com</a> for more details</span>
  <a data-text-id="16288567226310458971" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('HpTJImdz0MRAEVsMrtBh95J/dLKe6AMbQSVo3CHSlKnjqAxK00acQcZroRnquyWPzhIjj6KNyGtl1y5f30SUlQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('A5FYCtJPVhCCjX0GUFT2bbJ4Dij6AAc4POhNTcyq9Vn+rZ1iZnoalQT3hxMUP7IV7hVZFcZlzEgYGgvOMjz1ZQ==')})
  }
//]]>
